Comment

This file contains scanned images of a Well Completion Report submitted
under Australian Government legislation . The data in this file are made
available to assist future explorers for petroleum and may be distributed
freely .

Summary :

Barnett3 an exploration well tested a fourwaydip closure mapped in the Late Carboniferous to Early
74 Permian Kulshill Group . It is located in NTP28 in the offshore Bonaparte Gulf . The nearest well is
Barnett1 300m to the northeast .

The primary objective sands were at the top of the Kuriyippi formation . These were intersected 16m low
to prognosis and were of poor reservoir quality . Good fluorescence and brown oil seen in cuttings
throughout the Keyling Formation is considered to be residual or dead oil . No resistivity anomalies
were recognised and a comprehensive SFT program indicated water gradients for all zones . In the

1712 inch hole poor oil shows were recorded while drilling fossiliferous zones within shales of the
Fossil Head Formation .

Ll



















Barnett 3 reached a total depth of 1701m ( logger extrap ) 205m into sands of the upper Kuriyippi
Formation . The well was plugged and abandoned .

1.3 Drilling Summary

Daily drilling r ports are summarised b low and the drilling tim versus depth
curve is shown in figure 2 . Table 1 is the bit record .

REPORTS 1 AND 2
Tow rig to location

REPORT 3 29890

Move onto location . Jack up and preload . Jack up to final height and rig up
prior to spud . ( MSLRKB 32.5m ) .

REPORT 4 30890

Complete rigging up . Run in 36 assembly and tag mudline at 52.6m RKB . Spud
w 11 at 0600 hours . Survey ( 0 degrees ) and drill 36 hole to 87m . Survey

( 1 degree ) and run in 30 casing to 87m . ( ST2 below ML ring ATD above ) .

C ment with 659 sacks of Class G cement with seawater and 0.64 CaC12 ( 2004
xcess ) .

REPOR 3110
Nipple up diverter and make up 26 BHA . Drill 26 hole to 170m noting partial

losses at 92m and total losses at 132m . From 148m stuck pipe became a problem
due to a coarse uncoordinated sand . Pipe was greed by pumping hivis slugs
back reaming and up to 200000 # overpull . Continue to wash and ream hole .

REPORT 6 010990

Continue washing and reaming 26 hole . Install jars in string . Pump
unyielded gel into the loose formation in an attempt to stabilise the caving
without success . Pump a 697 sack with 2.5 4 PHG cement slurry from 172m .
W.O.C .

REPORT 7 020990
Pump a second cement slurry ( 1196 sacks with 2.54 PHG ) and W.0O.C . Drill out

cement from 85m . 1004 returns dropping to 704 at 141m . Drill 26 hole to
241m spotting LCM slugs and control drilling ( 20mm ) . Losses to formation
approximately 20 bblshr .

REPORT

Drill 26 hole to 345m . Run survey ( 14 degree at 337m ) and perform check
trip before tripping out to run casing . Run 20 casing working and washing
through tight spots at 99m and from 279m to shoe depth at 333m . Circulate
casing and rig up to cement .

REPORT 040990

Cement 20 casing without obtaining cement returns . Cut casing and weld on
2114 bradenhead . Test bradenhead to 450 psi and casing to 600 psi before
rigging up diverter . Pick up the 1712 assembly and drill out the 20
shoe . Drill 1712 hole to 411m .

REPORT 10 10990 :

Drill 1712 hole to 580m using seawater PHG sweeps diluting and control
drilling to maintain mud weight below 9.2 ppg . Polymer additions to increase
yield point were necessary . A wiper trip from 580m to the 20 shoe was made
noting a maximum overpull of 40 kps . Drilled 1712 hole to 805m ( TD ) .

9082x


-----Page 15-----

.6

REPORT 11 09

Circulate and condition hole before performing wiper trip to 20 shoe . After
circulating hole clean ( 2m fill ) a survey was dripped and hi vis slug spotted
before pulling out to log .

Run # 1 MSFLDLLGR was run from 803m after repairing the HLS depth counter
( 112 hours ) . Run in to perform clean out trip before casing ( 2m fill ) .
Drop multishot and pull out of hole .

Run 66 joints of 1338 K55 casing setting shoe at 799m .

REPORT 12 070999
Run and cement 1338 casing at 799m using an 800 sack ( Class G with 2.54

bentonite ) lead and a 350 sack neat Class G tail . Bump plug and pr ssure
test casing to 2000 psi prior to cutting casing and installing the B
section . Nipple up 1358 BOP stack and successfully pressure test including
choke kill manifolds etc . Begin making up 1214 BHA .

REPORT 13 080990
Make up 1214 BHA including mil ! tooth bit ( Reed HP216S IADC217 ) junk

sub and 50 pendulum configuration and drill out shoe track plus 9m of open
hole . Displace the hole to KCLPHPA mud and perform leakoff test . 15.2 pppg
equivalent was reached without lead off . Drill 1214 hole to 1068m taking
single shot surveys at 984m and 1063m ( 12 percent at 1063m N20 E ) .
Circulate bottoms up and trip for bit change .

REPORT 14 090990

Pick up DBS PDC bit ( TD 290 ) and run in with a packed BHA . Ream last 100
metres . Drill 1214 hole to 1080m . Pull PDC bit due to low penetration
rate . Run in TCI gauge protected bit ( Smith F27D IADC 517 ) and packed BHA
with junk sub and drill 1214 hole to 1lllm .

REPORT 15 100990

Drill 1214 hole to 1203m noting extremely high torque ( 500 amps ) and slow
penetration . Run a single shot survey and trip to inspect bit and BHA at
1215m . Lay out junk sub and replace NB stabilizer and run in with new bit
( IADC 517 ) . Ream and wash final 100m to bottom .

REPORT 16 110990

Drill 1214 hole to 1346m and circulate hole clean for a single shot survey
at 1331m . Work stuck pipe free with 1500001b overpull . Drill 1214 hole
to 1388m .

REPORT 17 120990
Drill 1214 hole to 1445m . Wiper trip to 1088m to check hole condition .

Hole condition fine . Drill 1214 hole to 1460m . Very slow penetration
rates ( 2.5 to 3.6mhe ) .

REPORT 18 1309
Drill 1214 hole to 1495m and circulate up a sample at the drilling break

( 2mhr to 6mhr ) . Drill 1 metre to 1496 and circulate up a second sample
before tripping out of the hole to pick up the core barrel . Run in witha
stabilised 60 x 8 x 514 core barrel and PDC corehead ( 1214 DC502 ) .

9082x

REPORT 19 140990
Run in with 60 core barrel and cut 1214 x 514 core from 1496 to 1514n .

ROP slow at 2.5 mhr . Pull out core barr 1 and r cov r cor ( 964 ) . Run in
with same core barrel and core head and cut core no 2 from 1514 to 1520m .

REPORT 20 150999
Continue coring from 1520m to 1532m . ROPs varying from 0.9 mhr to 2.7mhr .

Pull out core barrel and lay out core no 2 ( 994 recovery ) . Pick up a TCI bit
( Smith F2 IADC 517 ) with a packed BHA and drill 1214 hole to 1632m .

REPORT 21 160990
Drill 1214 hole to 1633 m drip a survey and trip for bit change ( Smith F2

IADC 517 ) keeping packed BHA . Ream final 50m and drill 1214 hole to
1700m . TD Perform 5 stand wiper trip circulate hole clean drop survey and
pull out to log .

REPORT 22 170990

Rig up EHLS and run .

SUITE # 1 DLLMSFLGR TD TO 1338 CS
SUITE # 2 SLDCNSSGR TD TO 1338 CS
SUITE # 3 MELBCSGR TD TO 1338 CS
SUITE # 4 SET HP GAUGE FAILURE

Work on SFT tool ( replace HP gauge ) and rerun without success . Lay out SFT
and run log # 5 VSP .

REPORT 23 180990
Run 65 levels with velocity survey and rig down HSL . Pick up 1214 bit and

run in for wiper trip and condition mud and hole . Rig up HLS and run log # 6
six arm dipmeter . KRecover and work on dipmeter tool .

REPORT 24 190990
R pair dipmeter and run Suite # 6 from TD to 1338 CS .

Run Suite # 7 SFTHPGR . Take 47 pressures and recover 10 gallon sample from
1523m . ( Water ) .

REPORT 25 200990
Run Suite # 8 sidewall cores . Rig down HLS and RIH with OEDP for PS8A . Set

the following plugs :

# 1 1560 1430m Tag at 1418m
# 2 1130 1030m Tag at 1041m
# 3 835 735m Tag at 753m

REPORT 26 210990

Run in with 1338 casing cutter and make cut at 131m . Unable to circulate
1338 20 annulus . Recut 1338 casing at 100m . Nipple down BOPs and
recover wellhead ( B section ) and 1338 csg . Set plug # 4 from 160m to 56m .
Tag surface plug at 58m . Run in with casing cutter and cut 20 casing at 57m .

REPORT 28 230990

Skid in cantilever and secure rig for tow . Jack down and check for water

1.5 Drill Fluid Summary

The well was drilled with seawater with gel sweeps to 805m and with a KC1
polyacrilamide mud to 1700 m. Baroid mud report is contained in Appendix 5 .

9082x

GEOLOGY

-----Page 26-----

16

2 . GEOLOGY
2.1 Predrilling Summary and Rationale

Barnett3 was drilled primarily to evaluate the maximum flow potential of coil
sands at the top of the Kuriyippi Formation penetrated in Barnett2 300 m to
the northeast . 3D seismic mapping at the top of these sands ( 14.9 and 15.0
sands in Barnett2 ) showed that Barnett3 was located at the absolute time
crest of the structure . As secondary objective the well tested closures
mapped within the Keyling Formation and Treachery Shale . In Barnett1 and2
these intervals were not within closure .

The Barnett3 location was considered to be a potentially useful production
location in addition to Barnett2 .

Risks recognised prior to drilling Barnett3 included 1 ) stratigraphic
pinchout of reservoir sands or their subunconformity dip 2 ) poor reservoir
quality of reservoir sands and 3 ) structural prognosis low due to
unpredictable velocity gradient .

2.5 Cores

Two 18m 414 diam ter conventional cores wr cut back to back over the
interval 14961532m at the top of the Kuriyippi Formation . Recoveries wr
964 and 994 for cores 1 and 2 respectively . The cores recovered in
fibreglass sleeves were cut into one meter lengths and sent to Adelaide for
full description and standard core analysis by Gearhart Core Data Australia .
Lithological descriptions of meter core chips and whole cores are included
here . Gearhart Core Datas core report ( Appendix 1 ) includes results of
analysis of 57 plugs and core photography .

LOGGING AND SURVEY

-----Page 58-----

46

3 . L IN RVEY :
3.1 Mudlogging

Exploration Logging of Australia ( EXLOG ) provided mudlogging services from
345m to 1700m which included monitoring and reporting of depth rate of
penetration Dc exp sigma log lithology and shows calcimetry total gas
gas chromatography and H2S . In addition lag time pit levels pump strokes
@ Arilling parameters ( ROP weight on bit RPM ) bit performance surge and swab
pressures when tripping pore pressure ECD fracture gradient deviation and
casing weight were monitored .

Exlogs mudlogging report is included as Appendix 2 .

Exlog collected seven sets of washed and dried cuttings samples which wer
dispatched as follows :

1 set : N.T . Dept of Mines and Energy
1 set : BMR
5 sets : SANTOS

1 set of Samplex : SANTOS

These were collected every 10m below the 20 casing shoe and every 3m below
the 13.375 shoe .

Two sets of wet unwashed cuttings ( one bagged one canned ) were coll cted at
30m intervals below the 20 casing shoe . These were despatched to Santos for
storage at Gillman core library . ( One set of unwashed cuttings were also
collected at 10m intervals in the 17.5 section and 3m intervals in the
12.25 section and was despatched to the BMR .

3.2 Wireline Logging
Wireline logs were run by Haliburton Logging Services Ltd at the interm diate

TD of 805m in 1712 hole and at final TD of 1700m in 1225 hole . Logs and
intervals are listed below :

SUITE 1 RUN TOOLS INTERVAL

1 1 DLLMSFLBCSGRSPCAL 803.0 4.0m
2 1 DLLMSFLGRSPCAL 1700.7 798.7m
2 1 SLDCNSSGR 1700.7 798.9m
2 1 BCSMELGR 1701.4 798.7m
2 1 SFTGR 1581.8 798.7m
2 1 SEDGR 1701.0 798.7m

Wireline logs are not included here as they have been distributed under a
separate cover

9082x


-----Page 59-----

m47

3.3 Hole Deviation Surv ys

Smith International Australia Pty . Ltd. conducted a magn tic multishot survey
in the 1712 hole prior to running 1338 casing from 794m to surface .
Eight magnetic single shot surveys were recorded by the drilling crew at
approximately 100m intervals while drilling the 1214 hole . The results of
both surveys are included here and Smith International Australia Pty . Ltd.s
report follows .

3.4 Velocity Survey

Seismographic Services Ltd. carried out a static rig source Vertical Seismic
Profile ( VSP ) using an 80 cuin . airgun offset at 73.6m . Gun pressure was
constant at 1800 psi . Gun depth was changed from 9m to 7m after the 1250m KB
level was recorded due to the tide .

A total of 71 separate check levels were recorded between 1680m and 100m KB .

Seismographic Services Velocity Log Calibration Report and Vertical Seismic
Profile Report are included as Appendix 3 and Appendix 4 respectively .

WELL TESTING

Drili St m Tests ( DSTs )

No drill stem tests were conducted .

Sequencial Formation Tests ( SFT )

Sequencial formation tests ( SFT ) were attempted at 48 points 33 gave

stabilized pressures 11 were tight and 1 casing check was made . A

segregated fluid sample was taken at 1523.0m recovering 12 gals of
filtrate .

b. PROGNOSIS

Barnett3 was designed to test the oilbearing z20ones ncountered in
Barnett2 and to address a series of potential reservoirs in the
early Permian section above the known pay 20ne . Barnett2 failed to
test the crest of the Kuriyippi Formation and none of the shallo
units were penetrated within closure by either Barnett1 or 2
These wells were positioned to test the deeper Carboniferous

section .

Barnett is a domal anticlinal structure located on an eastwest
trend that includes the Turtle Neptune and Siren structures in the
southern portion of the Bonaparte Basin . A low amplitude keystone
graben within the Permian section has offset the crest in the
shallow section such that neither Barnett1 nor 2 were within
closure for any horizon above the midTreachery shale . Barnett3 is
located such that it will be a crestal test of these formations .

Source rocks in the Barnett region are in the rift and postrift
sequences of : the Devonianlate Carboniferous section . These
sequences contain a range of potential source material including
evaporites and both deep and shallow marine shales . The Barnett
reservoirs are much shallower in the section than the potential
source units implying that considerable vertical migration has
occurred which may have been assisted by the large normal faults in
the area and the generally sandy Kuriyippi Fm .

Exploration Logging provided a Data Monitoring Service from 172m
( within the 26 section ) to Total Depth at . 1700m . Formation Logging
commenced from the 20 casing shoe only at 345m . Continuous
evaluation of pressure and drilling progress from realtime da !
provided an aid in optimizing drilling costs . ensuring drilli ..
continued with maximum safety to personnel the well and equipment ..
The operator was continuously 4dvised as to the status of these
analyses . The printouts and plots of the results and services are
contained in the appendices to this report .

2 . PRILLING AND ENGINEERING
a . Well History

The Marsk Valiant jackup rig arrived on the Barnett3 location at
09:00 hours on August 29th 1990 . Mean seawater depth was 19m and
drill floor to seabed was 52.6m . All depths are in metres below the
drill floor unless otherwise stated . i

36 Hole Section : 52 to B8 metres

The drill floor was cantilevered into positioned and the seafloor
tagged at 52.6m . A survey established 0 inclination . The well was
spudded at 0600 hrs on the 30th August with NB # 1 a Security S35J
26 in tandem with a 36 holeopener . This assembly drilled 3f
hole to 87m ( 26 to 68m ) in 3.0 hrs at an average rate of
penetration of 12 mhr utilising seawater with returns to the
seafloor . A 50 bbl hivis pill was pumped a survey run ( 1 at
84m ) followed by a wiper trip to the mudline . Only 0.5m of fill
was noted on the trip in . A further 20 bbls of hivis mud was
pumped and the assembly was tripped .

Casing ( 30 310 ppf 68 joints ) was run and landed with th shoe at
87m . It was cemented with 647 sx of ( G grade cement at 1.89 sg
slurry density . The diverter assembly was then installed .

26 Hole Section : B8 to 345 metres

RRB # 1.1 a 26 Security S35J drilled the 30 casing shoe and
cleaned the rathole to 88m . New formation was drilled to 92m with
spud mud where partial loss of returns occurred . Full losses
occurred at 96m but again partial returns were regained from 114m .
The drilling fluid was altered to seawater from 100m with hivis
sweeps every 9m . A 25 bbl LCM pill was pumped at 132m in an attempt
to minimise losses . At . 148m the pipe became stuck but was worked
free . The drilling fluid was again altered to a closed system
utilising spud mud . Drilling continued to 170m where a connection
was attempted with the pipe becoming stuck at 160m . The pipe was
worked a 200 bbl hivis pili was circulated but the pipe could
not be worked back further than 158m ( maximum overpull of 350 kib ) .
A set of surface jars were made up to the drillstring and . while
making up these jars the pipe freed itself . The string was back
reamed without circulation to the shoe at 87m . An unsuccessful
attempt was made to break circulation and the bit was tripped . The
Jets were found to be blocked by quartz gravel .

RRB8 # 1.2 was run in but was unable to pass below 88m . The bit was
washedreamed to 114m with partial returns . A short trip was made
to include jars and further 8 drill collars to the BHA . The
reaming continued to 147m where 120 bbls of unyielded gel 450 bbls
of spud mud and 50 bbls of LCM were pumped . A short trip was then
made to the casing shoe with the bit being run back to 147m without
difficulty . A further 200 bbls of unyielded gel and 100 bbls of
spud mud were circulated while washing to 155m . Full circulation
was lost at this point . The bit was washed to 170m with 2 more
unyielded gel pills circulated ( 120 and 200 bbls ) . Only 2m of new

SANTOS Ltd 3


-----Page 128-----

formation was drilled on this run to 172m . A 150 bbl unyielded gel
pill was spotted on bottom and the bit was tripped .

A stinger on openended drillpipe was run to 172m but circulation
could not be established . The string was pulled and the stinger
clear d of gravel fill . It was rerun tagged bottom and c ment
Plug1 was mixed and pumped . It was pulled back to the sho to wai

on cement then run in again tagging the top of the plug at 133m .
Plug2 was then mixed and pumped prior to tripping out .

RRB1.3 tagged cement at 85m then drilled firm cement to 123m with
85X returns . From 123172m soft cement was drilled at over 50 mhr
with 60704 returns . New formation was drilled with initial mud
losses of over 200 bblhr . The use of LCM decreased this loss to
under 100 bblhr . At 208m the noz21es became blocked after a
connection was made and the string had to be tripped when they
could not be cleared by surging the pipe . They were found to be
blocked by LCM which was cleared and one jet was removed prior to
tripping in .

RRB1.4 recommenced controlled drilling ( average 20 mhr ) to the
final casing depth of 345m . Mud losses to the formation were
initially 80 bblhr but these decreased to 20 bblhr after further
addition of LCM . A closed mud system of seawatergel was utilised
on this final run . A troublefree wiper trip was made prior to
tripping out with no drag . The survey taken was a misrun . The bit
was tripped to bottom with no tight hole or fill tagged . The string
was tripped out after circulating returns and ruming a survey
( 0.75 at 337m ) .

Casing ( 28 joints 94 and 133 1lbft 20 ) was run to 279m with
only one minor tight spot noted at 99m . Mud losses of 50 bbls were
recorded to this point which equates to losses of 8 bblhi
consistent with the losses of 5 bblhr recorded while the casing
running tools were being made up . The casing was worked through
279289m and had to be washed from 289m to the final setting depth
of 333m . The hole was circulated clean with mud losses of 15 bblhr
noted . A cement stinger assembly was run in and the casing was
cemented with a lead slurry of 600 sx of G cement ( with 2.54 pre
hydrated gel ) at 1.46 sg . The tail comprised 500 sx of ( G grade
cement neat at 1.90 sg . The stinger assembly was tripped out . the
MLS ports were opened and circulation was established through the
wash ports ( no cement returns were seen ) . The casing was cut the
bradenhead installed and the diverter assembly was nippled up and
pressuretested .

17.5 Hole Section : 345 to 805 metres

NB2 a Reed MS513G 17.5 tagged cement at 331m . It drilled cement
the shoe at 333m and cleaned the rathole to 345m before drilling
ahead . A basic seawatergel mud system was in use with an initial
density of 1.09 sg .

The rate of penetration was controlled to a large extent with a

target maximum of 30 mhr . This was occassionally exceeded even
with greatly reduced weightonbit through the loose sands found

SANTOS Ltd 4


-----Page 129-----

below 510m . At 580m a wiper trip to the 20 casing shoe was run
which gave nil to 30 klb overpull only . The Bi kat 30m was

precautionary reamed before drilling recommenc d. The rate of
penetration continued at 1040 mhr to 735m where it fell to below
20 mhr then further still as increasingly argillaceous sediments
w re penetrated . The drilling fluid required largescale dilution
to maintain the density at 1.10 se . At 805m casing point was
reached and returns were circulated . A wiper trip to the 20 casing
shoe was made which gave drag to a maximum of 80 klb . The bit was
run back to 795m and 10m of fill was tagged prior to circulating
returns . Another 9 stand wiper trip was made to 580m with only 2m
of fil1 noted . Again returns were circulated prior to tripping out
with no overpull recorded . A survey indicated a hole angle of 0.5
at 803m .

The following wireline logs were run : DLLMSFLBCSGRSPCal

RRB2.1 was used on a conditioning trip prior to running casing . It
washed 2m of fill followed by 3 full circulations . The trip out
gave no overpull . A magnetic multishot survey was run on the trip
out but this only produced a profile up the borehole to 333m as it

Was incapable to produce azimuth readings within the 20 casing .

This resulted in a relatively large degree of uncertainty in the
bottomhole position .

Casing ( 67 joints . 13.375 68 ppf ) was run and landed with the
shoe at 799m . It was cemented by a lead slurry of 800 sx Class G
neat at 1.50 sg slurry density . This was followed by 300 sx of
Class G at 1.90 sg . This was displaced and the wiper plug was
seated with 2000 psi . There were no mud losses while pumping or
displacing the cement . The casing was pressuretested to 2000 psi
then cut and the BOPs installed and pressuretested to SANTOS
specifications .

12.25 Hole Section : 805 to 1700 metres .

NB3 a Reed HP21GJ 12.25 drilled cement in the casing from 773m
the shoe at 799m the rathole to 805m and new formation to 808m .
While drilling new hole the seawatergel mud system was displaced
to a KClPrehydrated Polyacrilamide ( KCIPHPA ) system at an
initial density of 1.07 sg . An FIT was run which with an imposed
pressure of 5929 kPa . produced a fracture pressure gradient of 1.82
sg EMD . Drilling continued at an average 12 mhr with an elevated
background gas of 0.24 . This is believed to be derived from
degradation of the Polyacrilamide fraction of the new mud system
( the chromatograph breakdown indicated a background of only
0.006X4 ) . Drilling continued at 917 mhr through claystone to 831m .

The secondary objective was intersected at 831m with a drillbreak
to 48 mhr . This was flowchecked before continuing drilling at 30
50 mhr . To maximise formation evaluation as well as to not
overload the annulus controlled drilling was initiated with a
target average . of 2025 mbr ( although instantaneous rates
occassionally attained 50 mhr ) . At 1060m the rate of penetration
fell below 20 mhr consistently and the bit was tripped at 1068m .
No overpull was recorded on the trip out . The bit was graded T5 B4

SANTOS Ltd 5


-----Page 130-----

G0 . A singl shot survey indicated a hole angle of 0.5 ( Azimuth
20 ) at 1063m .

NB4 a Diamant Boart Stratabit TD290 12.25 was made up to a BHA
that had 3 nearbit stabilisers ( within 16m ) and a foutth 63m
above . It was run to 966m and reamedwashed to bottom . No trip ga
was recorded . Drilling commenced at 1530 mhr but decreased t
less than 5 mhr below 1074m through a strongly cemented sandstone .
There appeared to be an abundance of rock flour in the cuttings
which was indicative of inefficient hydraulics though this may
have been a product of the cutting action of this style bit . By
1080m torque was fluctuating rapidly from 2.4 to over 13 kft.lbs
at a penetration rate of only 0.8 mhr and the bit was tripped .
Minor overpull was noted on the trip out . The bit was graded as
only 5k worn and ingauge .

NB5 a Smith F27D 12.25 was made up to the same packed BHA and
washed from 10601080m before drilling ahead at 17 mhr through
the same calcareous sandstone . Trip gas was nil . Torque was again
: extremely variable regularly stalling the rotary drive . At 1124m
a drill break to 50 mhr was flowchecked before drilling ahead .
The high torque persisted and the rate of penetration was variable
being dependent on whether or not weight could be applied to the
bit ( increasing WOB commonly stalled the rotary drive ) . At 1215m
returns were circulated and the string was tripped troublefree .
The junksub was removed from the BHA and an undergauge nearbit
stabiliser was exchanged .

NB6 a Smith F2 12.25 was tripped in to 1107m and reamedwashed
to 1215m . Drilling resumed with vastly reduced torque at a
controlled average of 2025 mhr . Below 1310m the controlled
drilling was no longer required as the formation had altered
dominantly siltstone and claystone with rates of penetration belo
10 mhr . At 1346m while circulating prior to running a singleshot
survey the pipe became stuck at 1322m . It was worked with a
maximum of 120 klb overpulil and finally Jjarred free . The survey was
run successfully ( 0.75 at 110 azimuth ) a connection made without
problem and drilling resumed to 1445m where a 13 stand wiper trip
was made to 1088m . No overpull or fill was noted . Drilling again
continued at 2.55 mhr to 1494m where an increase in penetration
rate was noted to a maximum of 7.4 mhr . Returns were circulated at
1496m and the bit was then tripped to commence coring . The trip out
was troublefree and a survey run indicated a hole angle of 1 at
1476m ( Azimuth 507 ) .

CB7 a Diamant Boart Stratabit CD502 12.25 was made up to an 18m
core barrel and run to 1466m . The section 14661494m was washed and
the final 2m was reamed before coring commenced at an initial rate
of penetration varying from 523 mhr . This decreased to below 2
mhr but the full 18m was cut before tripping out . Core1 was cut
from 14961514m in 6.8 hrs and 17.34m was recovered ( 986.34 ) . The
trip out was troublefree .

RRCB7.1 was run and washed the final 28m to bottom before coring
commenced at less than 2 mhr . The majority of the core was drilled
at this rate except for the final 2.5 mhr where it increased to an

SANTOS Ltd 6


-----Page 131-----

average 16 mhr . The assembly was tripped troublefree after 18m
had been cut in 12.0 hrs onbottom . Recovery of Core2 was 17.8m
( 98.9k ) . As th basal section of Core2 appeared to be wat rwet
it was decided to terminate coring .

NB8 a Smith F2 12.25 washed through the core rathole from 1496
1532m without difficulty . Drilling recommenced at an averag . 15
mhr to 1628m where high and extremely erratic torque stall d the
rotary system forcing the bit offbottom . This persisted to 1633m
where the bit was tripped . A singleshot survey gave a hole angle
of 1.5 ( azimuth 40 ) . The bit was seen to be 0.19 undergauge
when recovered and the stabilisers were also well worn ( the near
bit stabiliser was replaced ) . A nearbit rollerreamer was
unavailable otherwise it would have been utilised in plac of the

stabiliser .

NB9 a Reed HP53AJ 12.25 was run to 1580m reamedwashed to

without danger of stalling the rotary system . The penetration rate
continually varied to a maximum of 20 mhr dependent on whether
or not the bit could be kept on bottom with optimum WOB and RPM .

At 20:30 hrs on the 16th September Total depth of 1700m was
attained . A 5 stand wiper trip was made which gave no drag . The bit

b . Bit Optimisation

Bit performance was continuously monitored and the operator advised
of cost p rformance rate of penetration torque and formation
changes . Cost analysis was performed on the basis of bit cost rig
cost and averag tripping sp ed . Plotted r sults are available in
Appendix F. No bits were tripped on a costmetre criteria . T

36 Hole Section

The 36 hole section was drilled with one 26 bit in tandem with a
36 holeopener in 3.0 hours averaging 12 mhr . It was considered

reusable .

26 Hole Section

The 26 hole section was drilled with one 26 bit a Security 535J
( IADC 136 rerun from the 36 section ) in 16.6 hours averaging
15.5 mhr . It completed this section in four runs . The first and
third runs were terminated due to blocked no2zles . The second was
terminated after only 2m were drilled to set cement plugs . The
fourth and final run was ended at the 20 casing depth .

17.5 Hole Section

The 17.5 section was completed with one bit only ( IADC 136 )
drilling the 460m in 21.9 hrs ( onbottom rotating ) at an average
rate of penetration of 21.0 mhr . Much of this section was control
drilled and the final grade of T2 B3 G0 indicates the generally
nonabrasive nature of this section .

12.25 Section

The 12.25 section was drilled with 7 bits in 8 runs . The
comprised of 1 militooth bit 4 insert bits 1 PCDstyle bit and 1
corehead ( run twice ) .

NB3 a milltooth bit ( IADC 136 ) drilled cement the shoe and 263m
of formation at an average penetration rate of 21 mhr . Much of
this section was controldrilled though instantaneous rates up to
60 mhr were recorded . This section appeared to be nonabrasive but
the tooth grade of T5 appears to indicate otherwise . On an offset
well a softer formation bit ( IADC 111 ) achieved over 400m with a
final grade of T8 . It is possible that NB3 may have reached that
footage with at least a similar grade indicating that in this
section the formation appears more cemented or abrasive .

NB4 a FPCD bit with a flatface profile drilled only 12m at 3.5
mhr before its run was terminated . Progress : through the
calcareous sandstone intersected was below 1 mhr at . the end of the
run and torque was extremely high and variable . Wear was
negligible ( 54 ) indicating that it was unsuited to this formation .

NB5 an insert bit ( IADC 527 ) progressed marginally faster through
the calcareous sandstone that held up the previous run . Weighton
bit of almost 50 klb was required to produce rates of 16 mhr . The
highly variable torque suggested the stabilisers were hanging vp in

SANTOS Ltd 8


-----Page 133-----

the borehole preventing full effective WOB being transmitted to the
drill bit . It was believed that the flexibility of the junksub was
allowing the bit to walk but the packed assembly was then having
to ream this slightly deviated hole . It was tripped after 135m were
drilled in 20.1 hrs at an average of only 6.7 mhr .

NB6 an insert bit ( IADC 517 ) was made up to a BHA minus the junk
sub and commenced drilling at 1550 mhr . Torque was relatively
low and stable from the commencement of this run . The penetration
rate decreased from 1326m to consistently below 10m mhr
( averaging 4 mhr only ) . The run was terminated to commence coring
after 281m were drilled in 53.5 hrs ( onbottom ) . Much of the
formation intersected consisted of claystones and siltstones with
only the upper sandstone section appearing to be abrasive . The
final bit grade of B6 is not surprising considering the moderately
high bit hours of 53 . It had been considered rerunning NB4 the
PCD bit through this section due to its high penetration rate over
a similar section in Barnett2 and it is most tikely it would have

performed as expected .

CB7 a PCD corehead cut the 18m of Core1 in 6.8 hrs . It was
graded as 104 worn and was subsequently rerun . RRCB7.1 cut the 18m
of Core2 in 12.0 hrs and was graded 154 worn . This bit did not
appear to be well suited to the hard cemented tight sandstones
and siltstones in the cored interval . The expectation was that
reservoirquality sands would be present and it must be borne in
mind that even thoveh the average rate of penetration was below 3
mhr it ranged from 0.7 to 22 mhr .

NB8 an insert bit ( IADC 527 ) only drilled 100m before high and
erratic torque forced a bit trip to inspect the stabilisers . These
were found to be severely undergauge as was surprisingly the
bit . Barring the final 45 metres of this run where the string was
worked hoping to overcome the torque problem . an average rate of
penetration of 14 mhr had been achieved . This was through sands
and silts that appeared moderately abrasive onlw as seen in the

cuttings .

NB9 another insert bit ( IADC 537 ) completed the final 67m to
Total Depth with similar torque problems . The drill cuttings
indicated increased cementation in this section . with a tendency
for grainsize reduction which would lead to increased
abrasiveness . This was borne out by the fact that this bit was
graded 0.25 undergauge after only 67m were drilled .

SANTOS Ltd 9


-----Page 134-----

c. Hydraulics Analysis

Hydraulics analyses were performed for the operator on a daily
basis and as requ sted . A printout of daily hydraulics data is
provided in Appendix K. A summary of hydraulics data in tabulated
form is provid d in Table 5 .

The rig was fitted with two Oilwell A1700 PT triplex pumps with LK !
12 stroke . This coupled with 6.5 liners produced an output of
4.98 galstk at 97X efficiency .

36 Hole Section

These sections of the hole were drilled with seawater and high
viscosity ( hivis ) sweeps . This was intended to prevent overloading
the annulus and maintain good hole cleaning .

26 Hole Section

This section was commenced with seawater and hivis gel sweeps .
High flow rates were inadequate to efficiently remove the coarse
river gravels intersected below 140m ( estimated ) . The drill flvid
was converted to a closed seawatergel system below 170m offering
improved carrying capacity . However this was offset by the forced
removal of one of the size18 nozzles ( left open ) as jet blockage
occurred with the use of LCM . This obviously created suboptimal
hydraulics for the final 139m of this section .

17.5 Hole Section

This section was drilled utilising a seawatergel mud system with a
density range of 1.091.11 sg . Large nozzles ( 2x2028 ) were selected
which produced suboptimal bit hydraulics but the high annula
velocities utilised ensure adequate holecleaning and this was the
prime requisite . Nozzle selection on the basis of optimising bit
hydraulics would have been pointless as the section was control
drilled to a large extent to prevent overloading the annulus .

12.25 Hole Section

The cement and shoe were drilled with the seawaterpolymer from the
previous section . With the intersection of new formation this was
displaced to a KC ) PHPA system at an initial density of 1.07 sg .
Several circulations were required to shear this fluid throueh the
bit and enhance the rheology . Initial hydraulics calculations .
using the PV and YP values recorded at surface produced total
pressure losses 4100 kPa in excess of actual standpipe pressure .
Within 24 hours of circulation this discrepancy disappeared . It
would seem that this initial departure from theoretical is a
function of the polyacrilamide that requires substantial shearing
through the bit before the surface PV and YP values reflect true
rheology at the bit .

Nozzle selection produced relatively high impact force and
hydraulic power at the bit . Flow rates to 1110m produced maximum
annular velocities that were above critical velocities promoting
hole washout . Below 1110m rates were reduced such that a laminar

SANTOS td 10


-----Page 135-----

flow regime was maintained . In the lower portion of this section
prior to coring the flow rate was reduced for mechanical
consideration of surface equipment but bit efficiency did not
appear to suffer markedly and cuttings transport was always optimal
with respect to both rheology and slip velocity .

d. Borehole Condition

Borehole condition was monitored during th drilling of Bamett3
by the obs rvation of ov rpull on trips and the observation of
hol fill after tripping . Carbides wer us d to evaluate average
open hole size . While drilling torque was constantly recorded to
determine other tight hole problems . @

36 Hole Section

No problems were encountered while drilling the 36 section or
running the 30 casing .

26 Hole Section

While drilling the 26 section full returns were observed to 92m
from which point they ranged from nil to partial only . The use of
LCM pills never resulted in full returns being established even
momentarily . At best it allowed the level in the amulus to
stabilise just below the flowline .

Stuck pipe and tight hole was a severe problem below 148m and would
appear to be related to the presence of river gravel beds which are
prone to collapse packingoff the string . Two cement plugs were
set from 88172m to stabilise this section of hole and to stem the
lost circulation .

After the cement plugs were set and further addition of LCM mud
losses finally stabilised to 20 bblhr in the lower portion of this
hole section . No overpull or fill was noted on the trip at casing
depth in this section .

The 20 casing was run to 279m without difficulty excluding
minor tight spot at 99m . However from 279m it had to be washed an
worked to the final shoe setting depth of 333m .

17.5 Hole Section

i
There were no hole problems while drilling this section . There were
no lost circulation 2o0ones and no drag was noted on comections .
High annular velocities maintained a relatively clean annulus .

A wiper trip at 580m did produce minor drag ( to 30 kilb ) and no fill
was detected . At casing point a wiper trip to the 20 casing shoe
gave minimal drag to 20 klb to 724m . From 724494m overpull of 40
80 klb was recorded and 2040 klb from there to the shoe . Fill of
10m was tagged and circulated out . A second wiper trip to 580m gave
negligible overpull and only 2m of fill was noted . Following the
wireline logs another conditioning trip was made which washed 2m
of fill . Three full circulations conditioned the mud prior to
tripping out with no overpull recorded .

The 13.375 casing was run and landed without problems . The cement
programme was completed with no mud losses to the formation .

SANTOS Ltd 12


-----Page 137-----

12.25 Hole Section

The section to 1346m presented no problems . Torque was low and
stabl cavings were minimal and no tight hole was recorded on
connections . At 1346m however while circulating prior to running a
singl shot survey the pipe became stuck at 1322m . It was jarred
free after working the string with a maximum overpull of 120 klb .
Connections below this were troublefree .

Both wiper trips and bit trips to Total Depth proved to be also
troublefree . Drag was never noted and fill was neeligible . Torque
through much of this lower section was variable and moderately high
but at 1628m it increased to a level at which the bit was unable
to be kept on bottom with optimum WOB without stalling the rotary
system . When retrieved the bit and nearbit stabiliser were both
seen to be out of gauge . They were both replaced and drilling
continued with the same torque problems to Total Depth . The use of
a rollerreamer may have ameliorated this problem but none suitable

was available .

The wireline logs found no difficulty in reaching Total Depth and
the caliper logs confirmed carbide data in that the upper section
was washed out to 1415 ( 23 avergauge ) while the lower section
was generally close to bit diameter .

3 . PRESSURE EVALUATION

a . Formation Fracture Pressure

Formation fracture pressures were calculated during drilling and
recorded in the Morning Reports ( Appendix K ) . Plotted data can be
found in Appendix D. Overburden egradients were calculated from
wireline density data and estimated OBG values were utilized while
drilling .

Only one Formation Integrity Test was run :

HOLE DEPTH HOLE CASING SHOE MUD DENS FRAC PRESS
( m ) Size ( m ) ( 56 ) ( 56 ) ( kPa )

808 12.25 799 1.07 1.82 5929

The 36 section was drilled with returns to the seafloor and no
estimate of fracture pressures is possible .

The 26 section encountered lost circulation from 96m and though
it was regained with the setting of cement plugs at 172m partial
losses persisted to casing point . The unconsolidated sands and
river gravels in the upper segment were the likely loss zones due
to their high permeability rather than hydraulic fracturing .

Although large volume losses were recorded while drilling the 17.5
section these were all attributable to a combination of new
hole drilled and surface solids control equipment .

There were no mud losses recorded in the 12.25 hole section that
were attributable to losses to the formation . The minimum estimated
fracture pressure of 1.55 2g EMD was never exceeded by either the
mud density or the circulating density .

SANTOS Ltd 14


-----Page 139-----

b . Formation Pore Pressure

Formation pore pressure indicators were monitored on a continu :
basis while drilling and pore pressure estimates were reported ..
the operator on a daily basis and when significant variations were
encountered . Plots of the relevant pore pressure indicators are
available in Appendix C and estimated pore pressure is plotted on
the Pressure Evaluation Log in Appendix D .
A normal formation pore pressure of 1.02 SG was assumed for
Barnett3 based on offset well data .

Returns from the 36 hole section were to the seabed and those in
the 26 section were not logged .

Due to the highly variable and arenaceous nature of the formation
the Dexponent Dxc is of little use in predicting any changes in
formation pore pressure . Mud temperature trends in the 17.5 hole
were masked by largescale dilutions and additions . Gas readings
were negligible ( 00.014 ) through the majority of this s ction . No
connection or trip gases were recorded . On the basis of this data
the estimated formation pressure was considered normal at 1.02 sg
to the 13.375 casing shoe . .

The 12.25 section also proved difficult to quantify pore pressure
parameters due to a variety of factors . Large scale volume
additions in the early portion masked any significant flowline
temperature variations . The highly variable lithologies ( eg silt
content and cementation even within relatively uniform membi )
produced excessive scatter on the Dxc plot and made trend lines
difficult to ascertain . Initial background gas in this interval was
high due to the degradation of basic drilling fluid constituents
rather than because of drilled gas . This forced a reliance on
chromatograph analysis of any deviation from this background .
However because of the paucity of even the lighter hydrocarbons in
this structure ( see Barnett1 and 2 mudlogs ) this proved a
difficult task . Trip gas values were all nil based on both Total
Gas and Chromatograph analysis .

Hole condition with regard to drag on connections and trips was
minimal . Tight hole was experienced while drilling below 1628m

but this a function of boreholestabiliser interaction in an under
gauge hole ( due to highly abrasive sandstones creating an under

gauge bit ) .

6 . DATA INVENTORY

The following were supplied to Santos Ltd at the wellsite on a
daily basis or as required :

1 copy Formation Evaluation Log

1 copy Drilling Data Plot 1:1000

1 copy Drilling Data Print

1 copy Costmetre Data Plot 1:1000
1 copy Pressure Plot

In addition a transmission system was employed which allowed all
data to be made available to Santos Ltd ( Adelaide ) on a daily
basis or as required .

On completion of the well all worksheets and charts were forwarded
to Santos . Four copies of the Final Well Report were compiled by
Exlog in Perth . Three copies of the report .. the log master copies
and a data disk in ASCII format were forwarded to Santos .
Exploration Logging retained 1 copy of the Final Well Report and
data disks .

Exploration Logging will use all reasonable diligence to maintain
and store the listed information and items in a manner to
reasonably prevent damage or loss . Provided however Exploration
Logging assumes no responsibility for the loss damage or theft of
the items or the information contained herein and shall not be
liable to Operator in any such event irrespective of cause fault
or the active or passive negligence of Exploration Logging or its
employees .

-----Page 228-----

SANTOS LIMITED WELL : Bamett3

VELOCITY LOG CALIBRATION COMMENT

WELL GEOPHONE SURVEY

A static rig source Vertical Seismic Profile ( VSP ) survey was conducted in this well on 17th September
1990 . The source was an B0 cu.in . Bolt airgun located at an offset of 73.6m . The gun was initially
deployed at a depth of 9.0m but this was changed due to the large tidal variation to a depth of 7.0m
after the level at 1250m below KB had been recorded . The gun was operated at a constant pressure
of 1800 psi throughout the survey .

A total of 71 separate check levels were recorded between 1680m and 100m below KB .

Preliminary times were obtained by timing from the first break on the gun hydrophone signal to the first
break on the well geophone signal . These times were then modified using an automated trace alignment
procedure which gives improved timing accuracy stacking and alignment of traces in the VSP
processing .

The levels at 600m and 1200m below KB were recorded both on entering and leaving the well . The
levels shot on the way into the hole yielded similar times to the compatible levels shot as the tool was
pulled out of the hole . In order to maintain a more consistent waveform in the VSP processing only the
levels shot in sequence as the tool was pulled out of the hole have been inciuded in the stack of traces
for the alignment procedure .

The recorded well geophone signal is of variable quality . The amplitude of the first arrival varies
considerably and appears to be quite low in areas where the caliper log shows extensive washout
indicating that there were problems obtaining a good coupling between the well geophone and the
borehole wall in these regions . In addition the body of the data is degraded by a high amplitude high
frequency tube wave arrival . The check level at 100m below KB is distorted by high frequency noise
at the first arrival probably due to the presence of poorly bonded casing and this has not been included
in the processing .

A 100m depth interval has where possible been selected for the calculation of reliable interval velocities
and the same depths have been used in the sectional display of well geophone traces .

SONIC LOGS

With the exception of the section ot log between 497m and 507m below KB the sonic log is well
recorded . This section of log has been edited with a straight line at the general velocity of the adjacent
sections of log . There is also a gap in the sonic log between 793m and 800m below KB . This has been
edited in the same manner . The log has been reintegrated before calibration .

-----Page 229-----

Page 2
Santos Limited

LOG CALIBRATION

The log calibration is generally wel ! controlled by the check level data . The exception to this is between
1100m and 1200m below KB . In this area the check level times show considerable scatter . This is
thought to result from poor coupling of the well geophone to the borehole wall due to the hole being
oversize . The calibration has been formulated with less regard paid to specific trends in this area and
only the general trend of the points has been followed . This results in a single shift of 1.2 ust over

the entire log .

Processed By :

Ma

DESCRIPTION OF SHIFTS USED IN VELOCITY LOG CALIBRATION

THO TYPES OF SHIFT MAY BE APPLIED :
C1 ) SHIFTS TO LOHER VELOCITIES WHICH ARE APPLIED LINEARLY .
THESE SHIFTS ARE CALCULATED USING THE FORMULA i

TU ? Teo ( Ti Ted
Z2 2j

x 103

WHERE TL AND TC ARE THE TRAVEL TIMES TO A GIVEN CHECK LEVEL :
MEASURED FROM THE UELOCITY LOG . AND WELL GEOPHONE DATA RESPECTIVELY
AND HHERE 2 IS THE DE ? PTH OF THE CHECK LEVEL BELOW DATUun .

CTL 7C ) 1S EXPRESSED IN NS ( AS JN THE CALIBRATION CURUE ) AND THE
RESULTING LINEAR SHIFT 1S EKPRESSEZD IN USFT .

( 2 ) SHIFTS TO HIGHER VELOCITIES WHICH ARE APPLIED DIFFERENTIALLY

IN ORDER TO APPLY LARGER CORRECTIONS TO LOKER VELOCITY SECTIONS OF LOG .
THIS IS BASED ON THE ASSUMPTION THAT LOWER VELOCITY SECTIONS

OF LOG CONTRIBUTE MORE TRANSIT TIME ERRORS THAN HIGHER VELOCITY
SECTIONS DUE TO CAVING AND OTHER BOREHOLE EFFECTS .

ADDITIONALLY THIS TYPE OF SHIFT MAY BE RESTRICTED BY DEFINING A
BASELINE VALUE SUCH THAT SECTIONS OF LOG RECORDED AT A HIGHER
VELOCITY THAN THAT OF THE BASELINE WILL RECEIVE NGO SHIFT .

RESTRICTED DIFFERENTIAL SHIFTS ( UNRESTRICTED SHIFTS WILL HAVE
A BASELINE VALUE OF ZERO ) ARE CALCULATED USING THE FORMULA

( TCy Te ) ( Za Z4 ) X BASELINE VALUE X 1078
Ss X 1004

TU ( 2g Z4 ) X SASELINE VALUE . X 1073

WHERE 7C SND 7L ARE EXPRESSED IN SEZONOS AND THE BASELINE VALU

iS ZIXPRESSED IN USFT .

SANTOS LIMITED WELL : BARNETT3

NSP PROCESSING COMMENT

INTRODUCTION

The data for this weli was acquired during a single run into the hole on the 17th September 1990 . A 3
component borehole geophone was used to record the data but only the vertical component data has
been processed for this report . Data was recorded between 1680m and 460m below KB with a 20m
geophone interval . Additional levels were recorded at 400m 300m 200m . and 100m below KB .

The check level at 100m was distorted by noise and has been omitted from all processing . All other
levels have been included in the log calibration report . For the VSP processing only the levels with a
20m depth separation have been included . The spacing of the remaining levels was considered
inappropriate for VSP processing .

DATA ACQUISITION

The energy source for this survey was an 80 cu . in . Bolt airgun . This was located at an offset of 73.6m
from the welihead . The gun was initially deployed at a depth of 9.0m but this was changed to 7.0m after
the level at 1250m below KS had been recorded . The gun was operated at a constant pressure of 1800
psi . The well geophone was lowered into the borehole to a depth of 1680m below KB with shots on the
way into the hole at 600m and 1200m below KB . The tool was then raised out of the hole and data
recorded at 20m intervals up to 480m below KB . A 100m interval was then used between 400m and
100m below KB .

The recorded data is of variable quality . The amplitude of the first arrival varies considerably between
levels and the body of the data is distorted by a high amplitude high frequency tube wave .

DATA PREPARATION

The VSP was produced using the processing sequence indicated on the side labels adjoining each
display .

Preliminary times were picked from the first break on the gun hydrophone signal to the first break on
the well geophone signal . These manually picked times were then modified using an automated trace
alignment process applied to the tape data for improved stacking timing accuracy and alignment of the
waveform for VSP processing .

After stacking a source signature deconvolution has been applied to the data on a trace by trace basis
using an operator designed from the first 300ms of the recorded hydrophone signal . This operator was
chosen by studying the consistency of the hydrophone signals and picking a window which was
considered to be representative of the source signature . This process collapses the energy contained
in the source bubble into the first arrival and standardises the signal before processing .


-----Page 266-----

Page 2
Santos Limited

STACKED GEOPHONE DATA

In order to investigate the frequency content of the raw data an FK analysis was perlormed on the edited
stacked geophone data aligned at oneway time . This shows the various praminent wavefields in the
data together with the extent of their frequency bandwidth . In addition to these wavetields any noise
with a consistent frequency would appear in the display as a horizontal alignment . This FK analysis is
used to select the preliminary filter applied to the data to remove unwanted noise at the beginning of
the processing sequence . For this data a 3 570 90Hz filter has been used .

DOWNGOING WAVEFIELD

The estimate of the downwave was obtained by aligning the first arrival at 100ms and enhancing the data
in such a way as to show the continuity of the downgoing energy from trace to trace without distorting
any real variations due to structural changes . The waveform is reasonably consistent over the first

225ms of live data after which it tends to vary with depth .

The downgoing wavefield ( Display VB2 ) is supplied with a 4 640 60Hz filter to match the seismic line .
This display can be used to identify multiples in the seismic which have not been suppressed by

processing ( see Appendix 1 ) .
UPGOING WAVEFIELD

The enhanced downgoing wavefield as described above has been used in a subtraction process to
remove the downwave from the data leaving a first estimate of the upgoing wavefield ( Display VO ) .

A deterministic deconvolution has then been applied to the upgoing wavefield using the stabe portion
of the downgoing wavefield ( the first 225ms ) as an operator . The deconvolution is applied on a trace
by trace basis . A comparison of Displays VO and VE ( upgoing wavefield after deconvolution ) shows the
effectiveness of this process in removing reverberance from the VSP data .

The effectiveness of VSP deconvolution is also shown by Display VH . If the process has been
completely successful this display should show a zero phase wavelet at the first arrival followed by a
dead trace . In practice there will be a slow bulid up of peg leg muttipies outside the deconvolution
operator length and this will show as increasing amplitudes down the traces .

In order to enhance upgoing events in the upgoing wavefield median filter tests were performed . A
range of spatial fikers were applied to the data and a Oms trace dip was selected .

ta aika 7 bn AS Pana a a Ei


-----Page 267-----

Page 3
Santos Limited

FILTER DETEAMINATION

To help design filters for the displays the data has been transferred to FK space ai three stages during
the processing sequence and both preliminary and final filters have been selected accordingly . The
optimum fiker is chosen such that it is the least restrictive filter that can be applied to the upgoing
wavefield to remove noise whilst retaining the best possible resolution in the data . A 4 640 60Hz filter
has been selected as optimum tor this data . A full description of the use of FK transforms is included

in the appendices at the back of this book .

RESIDUAL WAVEFIELD

In order to show wavefields with alignments differing from the upgoing and downgoing wavefields which
may be present in the data the undeconvolved data with both upwaves and downwaves subtracted is

presented ( Display VI ) .
BRIEF DESCRIPTION OF DISPLAYS SUPPLIED

The VSP displays supplied are of two types . Displays included in the book report are intended as quality
control displays showing every major step in the processing sequence . The loose leaf displays are
intended as working copies and are supplied at scales to match the seismic line .

Processed By :

John Drabble

APPENDIX 1

Description of V.S.P . Displays

Vertical Well : Source at Well Head

Display VA ( Stacked Geophone Data at oneway time )

This display indicates the quality of the data used in the subsequent VSP
processing . The trace displayed for each geophone position is the result of
editing as appropriate and summing common depth traces the common depth
traces having undergone a trace alignment procedure ( based on cross correlation )
in order to obtain accurate alignment prior to summation .

Source signature deconvolution will have been applied to marine data unless
otherwisa stated using the gun hydrophone signal as source signature ...

Wavelet stabilisaticn may optionally have been applied to the data to remove
variations in source character : due to changing source conditions ( particularly
onshore ) andor a variation in geophone coupling .

A broad band filter will have been applied to this data in order to remove
noise without compromising the usable bandwidth of the data .

The polarity of this display is such that the first downgoing arrival is
plotted as a black peak . ( SEG normal polarity )

Display VA ( FK ) ( FK Display of Stacked Geophone Data at OneHay Time )

This display shows the stacked geophone data ( after source signature
deconvolution if appropriate ) at oneway time transformed into FK space .
This data is displayed as wave number ( K ) against frequency with variation
in colour indicating amplitude in dB below the maximum.amplitude .

A velocity alignment in TX space transforms cCo.an alignment in FK space
rotated through 907 the various wavefields ( i.e .. velocity alignments ) commonly
observed in TX space transform.into FK space as illustrated in Fig.1

The strongest wavefield will normally be the Downgoing wavefield and this

transformsyinto analignment from Zero wave number zero frequency sloping in
the positive wave . number direction . Significart velocity changes in .
wavwefield will result in multiple alignments in FK space although in practice .
it may not bepossible to differentiate between the different FK alignments

and the resulting event may : be smeared .

Concd ....


-----Page 299-----

The data may be split into sections before transformation in order to allow
better analysis . The likely reasons for treating the data in this way are :

to separate out areas of differing velocity differing data quality
differing geophone separation or differing bandwidth .

When alignments intercept the K tor tf axis they will wrap around . The
frequency at which the intercept occurs 1s the fundamental allas frequency
further alliasing will occur at harwmonics of this frequency .

It should be noted that the resolution of the VSP data after wavefield
separation is not limited by the fundamental alias frequency .

The effects of spatial aliasing on the data will be small and in particular
after application of nonlinear spatial filters ( i.e . our normal method of
enhancing the data ) the aliasing effects can be assumed to be negligible .

This display illustrates in a convenient form the various prominent wavefields
in the data together with the extent of their frequency bandwidths the general
noise level and specific noise problems . In addition to general data analysis
it 1s used to establish the usable bandwidth of the Downgoing Wavefield in
order to design the broad band preliminary filter applied to the data in

Display VA .

Display VB ( Downgoing Wavefield )

This display represents a series of downgoilng wavefields observed at successive
locations ( i.e . geophone positions ) in the borehole . This display is produced
by shifting the data as shown in Display VA so that the direct arrivals and
therefore the Downgoing Wavefield are aligned in time a spatial filter is
then applied to remove random noise and crossing wavefields .

The downgoing wavefield trace extracted for each geophone position describes
fully the multiple systems that will occur as a tall to a reflector at or

near that geophone position . A comparison of a downgoing wavefleld with a

reflection occurring at the same depth on the seismic section at the well
w111 reveal any residual multiple activity on the seismic section assoclated
with that particular reflector . For this exercise the observed polarity of
the reflection on the seismic section should be matched with the same polarity
first arrival on the VSP downgolng wavefield i.e . white trough matched to
white trough or black peak to black peak . In the same manner the downgoing
wavefield display can be correlated with the upgoing wavefield of Displays VC
and VD to establish the presence and origin of multiples within the VSP data .

Note that this display is provided in two forms :

H

display essentially shows the data from which the deconvolutfon operators
have been derived .

( a ) VBI : filtered with the broad band preliminary filter only . This

( b ) VB2 : filtered so that the bandwidth matches that of the selsmic data in
the zone of interest to enable identification of residual multiples in

the seismic data . This version is presented at the scale ( s ) of the
seismic section .

These displays are produced at both polaritles .
Contd ...


-----Page 300-----

Displays VC and VD ( Upgoing Wavefield at twoway time

before and after enhancement )

These displays show the Primary and Multiple activity observed at the borehole
location from the shallowest VSP geoaphone position to some way below the deepest
VSP geophone positlon ( and therefore normally some way below Total Depth of

the borehole ) .

The data shown on Display VD is that of Display VC after application of a
spatial filter this spatial filter will be the result of varlous trials and
will have been chosen to give the best enhancement of the upgoing events
( horizontal andor dipping ) observed in the data .

In marine data 1f source signature deconvolution has been applied then the
input wavelet will be zerophase and the wavelet contained in the data will be
zero phase modified by earth absorption and transmission loss effects ( i.e . mixed
phase ) .

In the case of onshore data 1f neither wavelet stablisation nor source signature
deconvolution has been applied then the source signature remains in the data .
Wavelet stabilisation can be carried out by shaping to any given wavelet we
would recommend however that all geophone data is transformed to the waveform
of a shallow geophone level . In this case then the source signature effectively
remains in the data but 1s made consistent from level to level .

Events that reach the timedepth curve are primary and their lithologic
significance can be established unequivocally by reference to the calibrated
velocity log . This comparison can be made using Display VG1 which contains the
data from Display VF and the calibrated velocity log at the scale ( s ) of the
seismic section . Multiples having their last bounce from a primary within the
range of the VSP may be identified by observing their termination in the data
at the same depth point at which the primary cuts the timedepth curve .

From this display any dip across the well location can be recognised by move
out of the primary event to shorter time as the geophone moves up the well

and away from the lithology creating the reflection . No azimuith of dip can be
computed from this display but truedip can be computed from a measurement of
the 4T against vertical depth increment . Unconformity may be recognised by

an abrupt change of moveout of adjacent primary events . Topographical features
updip away from the well may be recognised by an increase inthe AT or in the
termination of an event away fron the timedepth curve . Dip increasing
updip away from the well can be observed in the data however 1f dip is
decreasing updip ( i.e . crest of an anticline ) then the event in question will

disappear from the data .

This data will normally have been filtered using the optimunm filter designed
after FK analysis to determine the usable bandwidth of the upgoing wavefield .

These displays are produced az both polarities .

Contd ...


-----Page 301-----

Display VC ( FK ) ( FK Display of Upgoing Wavefield at
twoway time : before enhancement )

This display shows the Upgoing Wavefleld at twoway time transformed into FK
space . Any filter applied to the data before transformation will be detailed

on the side label .

General Comments on FK displays made under Display VA ( FK ) also apply to this
display .

Since the Upgoing Wavefield is aligned horizontally or nearhorizontally in
TX space ( unless there is steep dip across the Well location ) it is aligned

vertically through zero wave number in FK space .

This display together with Display VE ( FK ) is used to establish the usable
frequency bandwidth of the Upgoing Wavefield to ald design of the socalled
optimum filter applied to the data in Displays VC VD VE VF VGl and VH .

The optimum filter 1s the least restrictive filter that can be applied to the
Upgoing Wavefield to remove nolse whilst retaining good resolution of the data
in the zone of interest ( if the zone of interest is not known then it is
assumed to be just above T.D . of the well ) . For this reason the FK analysis
is performed on data within a window around the zone of interest . Additionally
the data is windowed in time so that the data close to the TimeDepth curve
where we would expect better resolution is analysed .

This analysis and the FK analysis of the Deconvolved Upgoing Wavefield indicate
the limits of the frequency bandwidth in the data . Based on these guidelines
filter trials will be carried out and the optimum filter chosen fron the resul :

Displays VE and VF ( Deconvolved Upgoing Wavefield at twoway time

before and after enhancement )

These displays show the data as in Display VC after application of deterministic
deconvolution using operators derived from the Downgoing Wavefield on a trace

by trace basis . The effect of the deconvolution will be to remove all reverberants
associated with at least one reflector above the geophone position from which

the downgoing wavefield has been extracted .

The deconvolution is applied in a spiking mode unless otherwise stated and
the phase of the resulting data will be a function of the filter applied after
deconvolution . This 1s normally a zero phase filter giving a zero phase result
and maximum resolution of the lithology within the band limits . At the clients
discretion any other phase filter can be utilised .

The data shown on Display VF is that of VE after enhancement by application of
a spatial filter as described for Display VD .

These displays describe the primary reflection response of the subsurface at
the borehole location within the limits of the depth range of the VSP geophone
positions and additionally the primary reflection response below the deepest
VSP level . When using this response the accurate prediction of acoustic
impedance variation below TD will depend on the geometry of the subsurface

below the deepest VSP level .
Contd ...


-----Page 302-----

This data will normally have been filtered using the optimum filter designed
after FK analysis to determine the usable bandwidth of the upgoing wavefield .

The comments on the effect of dip etc . made under Display VC and VD also apply
to this display . The dip can be simply calculated from Displays VE and VF

using either of the methods described in Appendix 2 contained with this enclosure .
Most programmable calculators can be programmed to allow these calculations to

be done very simply and quickly .

These displays are produced at both polarities .

Display VE ( FK ) ( FK Display of Deconvolved Upgoing Wavefi1eld
at twoway time before enhancement )

This display shows the Deconvolved Upgoing Wavefield at twoway time transformed
into FK space . Any filter applied to the data before transformation wili be

detailed on the side label .
All general Comments made under Display VC ( FK ) also apply to this display .

The same analysis window will be used in the FK transformation of both the
Upgoing and the Deconvolved Upgoing waveflelds the resulting displays VC ( FK )
and VE ( FK ) will mainly differ in areas of low amplitude on the VC ( FK ) display
which will be boosted during deconvolution .

Display VH ( Deconvolved Downgoing Wavefield at twoway time )

This display is included to indicate the wavelets that will reside in the
deconvolved upgoing wavefields of Displays VE and VF . It also serves to
illustrate how effective the inverse operator is at collapsing the downgoing
wavefield from which it has been designed . Reverberants with periods longer
than the operator length used will remain in this display and will indicate

some of the multiples that will be retained in displays VE and VF ( Deconvolved
Upgoing Wavefield ) . In order to afford a direct comparison in time with Displays
VE and VF the wavelets have been shifted to their twoway time position before
display . The sidelobe activity of the wavelets is most likely to be a function
of the filter applied after the application of the inverse operator . This

level of sidelobe will also be present in Displays VE and VF .

Display VI ( Residual Wavefield at oneway time )

In this display both the upgoing and downgoing wavefields have been removed .
Most VSP data contains many other events in addition to the vertical upgoing
and downgoing wavefields . Reflections from fault planes diffraction energy
from point diffractors near the borehole and mode converted shear ( SV ) energy
are some of the possible events which will be revealed by this display .
Additionally residual tube wave energy will also be identified when present .

The interpretation of these types of events are difficult except for diffraction
hyperbolae and some fault plane reflections .

contd ...


-----Page 303-----

The method for calculation of the distance of diffraction points from the well
1s described in Appendix 3 contatned with this enclosure .

This display is produced at SEG normal polarity only .

Display VG ( Interpreters Composite )

This display is designed for use in interpretation and ts therefore presented
at the scale ( s ) of the seismic section .

It contains the enhanced deconvolved upgoing wavfield the transposed deconvolved
upgoing wavefield ( see explanation below ) and the calibrated velocity log . If
Synthetic Seismogram processing has been carried out then this display will

also include the formation density log ( if available ) acoustic impedance log
reflection coefficient series and the Synthetic Seismogram responses Primaries
Without Transmission loss and Primaries plus short term multiples .

Note that all comments made in the description of Display VF are relevant to
the enhanced deconvolved upgoing wavefield included in this display .

Two versions of this display will normally be produced ( both at seismic scale ( s ) ) .

VG1 : Filtered using the optimum filter designed after FK analysis
to determine the usable bandwidth of the upgoing wavefield .

VG2 : Filtered with the filter used in seismic processing .

These displays are produced at both polarittes .

Transposed Deconvolved Upgoing Wavefield

The transposed display is obtained by shifting the deconvolved upgoing wavefield
data so that the timedepth curve is transposed to the left or right hand edge
of the display thereby moving events that cut the timedepth curve to the edge
of the display enabling easier comparison with the seismic section .

The Interpreters Composite Display ( VG ) contains two displays of the Cransposed
data with the timedepth curve repositioned at both the right and left edges
to enable comparison with the seismic section in both directions away from the

well .

This is done by producing a series of output traces ( typically 24 ) from a number
of corridor scans of the deconvolved upgoing wavefield . Each output trace is
composed of data from a series of small windows one for each input trace

taken along the slope of the first arrival curve .

The first scan on each trace is from the first arrival curve to the time of the
first arrival on the following ( deeper ) trace as shown in Fig.2 ( a ) and produces

output trace 1l as shown in Fig2 ( b ) .

Contd ...


-----Page 304-----

Second and subsequent corridors will be composed of a series of windows parallel
to the first arrival curve their start time being determined by the end time
of the previous corridor in each case as show in Fig.2 ( c ) .

The number of corridors will be the same as the number of output traces requested .

The last window for output trace will extend to the end of the data on the
deepest input trace for output trace 2 the last window will extend to the end
of data on the next to deepest input trace and so on .

This method of transposition of the deconvolved upgoing wavefield ensures that
all Primary reflections appear at true times and depths along the left hand ( or
right hand ) edge of the display in order to facilitate comparison of this data
with the relevant piece of seismic section .

Changes of dip indicated by changes of ST from trace to trace on an event

on the deconvolved upgoing wavefield display will be retained visually in this
transposed display but the amount of AT between traces will be altered slightly
any dip calculations therefore should be made from the deconvolved upgoing
wavefield display .

The number of transposed traces displayed will be variable dependent on dip
but will typically be 24 .

Display Polarities

Polarities of displays in the VSP report obey the SEG conventions throughout
and displays are labelled POLARITY SEG NORMAL or POLARITY SEG REVERSE as
applicable .

APPENDIX 2

N Calculation of Dip from VSP Data
Vertical Wells : Source at Well Head
Introduction

The angle of dip can be calculated from the hyperbolic curvature of primary
reflections observed on the VSP deconvolved upgoing wavefield .

In calculating dip as described below two assumptions are made :
1 . The dipping reflector is a planar uniform surface .

2 . The velocity of the material above the reflector can be regarded as
constant .

Derivation of Equations

Figure 1 shows reflections froma dipping interface recelved at two geophone
positions G ) and G9 in a vertical well . An image point is constructed such

Method of Calculation

To calculate the dip of any Primary reflection observed on VSP data we therefore
require tj t2 t3 and t. These values can be obtained from a combination of
the computation sheet and deconvolved upgoing Wavefield display as follows :

Given a dipping Primary reflection observed on the deconvolved upgoing
wavefield then choose a pair of geophone traces to be used in the dip
calculation .

We would advise that the estimate be made using data as close as possible
to the timedepth curve as the ST due to dip is at its greatest for any
given geophone spacing when the geophone is closest to the reflector in

question .

t : the oneway first arrival time at the deeper of the chosen
geophone positions can be obtained from the computation sheet
( t at relevant depth ) . Alternatively if the computation
sheet 1s not available the equivalent twoway time can be
measured from the deconvolved upgotng wavefield display ( time
at timedepth curve on relevant trace ) and halved this method
is less accurate .

t2 : the oneway first arrival time at the shallower of the chosen
geophone positions ( te at relevant depth on computation
sheet )

the time of the arrival of the reflection fron the dipping
horizon in question at the deeper of the chosen geophone
positions . This can be obtained from the deconvolved upgoing
wavefield by measuring the twoway time on the deeper chosen
trace to the reflection being examined and subtracting the
oneway first arrival time at the same geophone

( i.e . t )

measuring the twoway time to the reflection being examined
on the shallower of the chosen geophone traces and
subtracting t2 .

t4

By substituting these values ( t t2 t3 and t4 ) in equations 13 the angle
of dip Xx can be calculated . Note that azimuth of dip can not be calculated

from this data .

It is suggested that dip is calculated for a number of geophone pairs to give
an indication of the scatter on the dip estimate .

If the beds are not plane dipping then shorter segments of the reflector have
to be used Co determine the dip at any point with an increasing likelihood of
error . Alternatively the 4T can be smoothed by hand to give an average

dip estimate .

APPENDIX 3

Calculation of Distance of Diffraction Points from Well

Vertical Wells : Source at Well Head

Introduction

The distance of a diffraction point from the well can be calculated for a
hyperbolic diffraction event identified on VSP Display VI ( Residual Wavefield
at oneway time ) . The calculation is best done using displays in oneway time
as twoway time displays distort the orientation of the diffraction pattern .

Derivation of Equations

The calculation is based on the schematic diagram shown in figure 1 where G
represents the geophone positlon whose trace on VSP display VI ( Residual Wavefield )
shows the vertex of the diffraction hyperbola in question .

The equation can be solved for t and the offset distance calculated ( rt Vj ) .

It should be noted that compression waves travelling near horizontally between
the diffraction point and the well can only be detected by a horizontally
polarised geophone and conversely a vertically polarised geophone will only
detect the SV component of the horizontally travelling wave . The exact nature
of the wave motion which results from diffraction of this kind has not been
studied in the subsurface . It seems most likely that there is mode conversion
from a nearly vertical P to a nearly horizontal SV . However if this nearly
horizontal travel happens to be along or close to a formation boundary other
motions Such as the pseudoRayleigh wave may develop . For practical purposes
the assumption of mode conversion fron P to SV seems adequate and Vj2V can be
used where a compressional input source and a vertically polarised geophone

have been used .

from tables of elastic constantas for particular rock types or it may be
determined from a knowledge or an estimate of the Lube wave velocity according
